  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_60071163-65d3-473a-88be-14786e7a6828'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6226473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15581084030100011565">everyone loves this book. everyone remembers it being lovely when they were children. but if you read it again you may find it creepy. i do. the illustrations are beautiful, and the message i s'pose is charming. but my son and i both dislike it. he becomes rigid with boredom when i try to read this to him, and he has pretty good reading stamina for a 2.5 year old. he digs all the classics, but we agree that this book is actually somewhat spooky. the bunny is not really asking mommy to rescue him</span>
  <span id="freeText15581084030100011565" style="display:none">everyone loves this book. everyone remembers it being lovely when they were children. but if you read it again you may find it creepy. i do. the illustrations are beautiful, and the message i s'pose is charming. but my son and i both dislike it. he becomes rigid with boredom when i try to read this to him, and he has pretty good reading stamina for a 2.5 year old. he digs all the classics, but we agree that this book is actually somewhat spooky. the bunny is not really asking mommy to rescue him; he wants a little space and freedom. if bunny were to say, "how about i go down to the depths of hell to escape you?" mommy rabbit would reply, "than i shall morph into lucifer and gobble you up in my fiery flames of fire."</span>
  <a data-text-id="15581084030100011565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6954097907690392147">If Max's mother had followed him to Where the Wild Things Are, you would have this book - assuming she allowed him to cross the ocean.<br/><br/>This is the story of a baby bunny and his mother. In it, baby bunny presents a number of imaginary scenarios in which he gets a little bit of independence for himself via turning into a child, a boat, a fish, a bird, and so on. For each scenario, mother bunny counters with how she would immediately catch him no matter what. You're a fish? I'm there with my net. Yo</span>
  <span id="freeText6954097907690392147" style="display:none">If Max's mother had followed him to Where the Wild Things Are, you would have this book - assuming she allowed him to cross the ocean.<br /><br />This is the story of a baby bunny and his mother. In it, baby bunny presents a number of imaginary scenarios in which he gets a little bit of independence for himself via turning into a child, a boat, a fish, a bird, and so on. For each scenario, mother bunny counters with how she would immediately catch him no matter what. You're a fish? I'm there with my net. You're a boat? I'll be the wind and <i>blow you where I want you to go</i>.<br /><br />When the child psychiatrist John Bowlby explained that a secure attachment for children is created by parents who "whilst always encouraging their children's autonomy, are nonetheless available and responsive when called upon," I don't think this is what he had in mind. How much better if she had said "I will be a safe harbor to which you can always return."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11863714484702204218">4.5 stars. Beautiful illustrations of a mother rabbit and her son.   <span id="freeText11863714484702204218" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Beautiful illustrations of a mother rabbit and her son. I really liked the imagination of the scenes illustrated, the rabbit son sprouting wings and the rabbit mother becoming a tree was wonderful. <div id="review_2812549092" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2812549092" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2812549092?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=picture-books">picture-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=possessive-love">possessive-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2812549092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7347591305083693037">Now unlike many readers, I actually never did experience Margaret Wise Brown's <u>The Runaway Bunny</u> as a young child (because while as a child in Germany I did get Eric Carle and Maurice Sendak picture books read to me in German translation, Margaret Wise Brown's work was unknown to my family). And perhaps this is also one of the reasons why the book (and first encountering <u>The Runaway Bunny</u> as an older adult) actually feels a bit uncomfortable and even a trifle strange with regard to both the auth</span>
  <span id="freeText7347591305083693037" style="display:none">Now unlike many readers, I actually never did experience Margaret Wise Brown's <u>The Runaway Bunny</u> as a young child (because while as a child in Germany I did get Eric Carle and Maurice Sendak picture books read to me in German translation, Margaret Wise Brown's work was unknown to my family). And perhaps this is also one of the reasons why the book (and first encountering <u>The Runaway Bunny</u> as an older adult) actually feels a bit uncomfortable and even a trifle strange with regard to both the author's message and how her presented narrative unfolds. <br /><br />For while I do appreciate the mother rabbit's all encompassing love for her little son, the fact that she is obviously not in any way willing or able to grant him any kind of distance or freedom, that any attempts by the young bunny rabbit to assert himself, to run away a bit (to get some necessary distance from his mother) are going to be met by the mother rabbit chasing after, capturing her son and once again tying him totally to her and her passion for him, to and for me on a textual and narrational level, this makes <u>The Runaway Bunny</u> read as rather stalkery, like at best a tale of a total helicopter parent who cannot and will not even remotely consider leaving her son alone a bit, who basically has to always be near him, attached to him and know everything about him (and who will also actively thwart any attempts by her child at achieving a bit of distance, privacy and freedom). <br /><br />And thus, while I do appreciate that the combination of Margaret Wise Brown's text and Clement Hurd's accompanying illustrations are considered magical and a classic (and probably also full of fond childhood memories for many) and albeit that I have indeed found especially Hurd's pictures innovative, imaginative and sweetly detailed, I just cannot get over my personal negative feelings regarding <u>The Runaway Bunny</u> (and especially as an adult who as a college language instructor was in fact once stalked by an obsessive student) that Margaret Wise Brown's printed words (even if they do show and are indeed imbued with much love and feeling) are also possessive, obsessive and really in my opinion smack far too much of over- clinginess on the part of the rabbit mother (and are therefore also just a bit too creepy and with an inherently rather unhealthy and problematic message for my tastes).</span>
  <a data-text-id="7347591305083693037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2017968484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017968484" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2017968484?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=bedtime-stories">bedtime-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=picture-book">picture-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=1001-children-s-books">1001-children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=animal-books">animal-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=children-s-book">children-s-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=margaret-wise-brown">margaret-wise-brown</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017968484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15439802398341904996"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496449882i/22914328._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='Bunny' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>4.5 stars</i>
</b><br/><br/>After I had read Margaret Wise Brown’s popular children’s book “Goodnight Moon,” I wanted to read more of Margaret Wise Brown’s works and I happened to stumbled upon another one of her popular works called “The Runaway Bunny,” along with artwork by Clement Hurd. “The Runaway Bunny” is a truly cute story about the love shared between a parent and child that children will enjoy!<br/><br/>The story starts off with a little bunny wanting to run away from home and when he told his mother about it,</span>
  <span id="freeText15439802398341904996" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496449882i/22914328._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="Bunny" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>4.5 stars</i>
</b><br><br>After I had read Margaret Wise Brown’s popular children’s book “Goodnight Moon,” I wanted to read more of Margaret Wise Brown’s works and I happened to stumbled upon another one of her popular works called “The Runaway Bunny,” along with artwork by Clement Hurd. “The Runaway Bunny” is a truly cute story about the love shared between a parent and child that children will enjoy!<br><br>The story starts off with a little bunny wanting to run away from home and when he told his mother about it, his mother just said that she will come running after him, no matter where the little bunny will run off to!<br><br>I must admit that I cannot believe that I waited this long to read this classic children’s story about a love shared between a parent and a child! Margaret Wise Brown had done a great job at conveying a mother bunny’s devotion to her child as she is always pledging to follow her child to the ends of the earth, whether the bunny wants to become a rock on a mountain or a sailboat to escape from his mother. I also enjoyed the soothing tone of this book as the story never felt too chaotic or intense when dealing with the little bunny’s desire to run away and I always felt good when the mother bunny tries to comfort her child by telling him that she will always love him no matter what. Clement Hurd’s artwork is truly gorgeous and creative to look at, especially when there are transitions between the black and white artwork and the colorful artwork. I loved the fact that the scenes where we get to see the imaginations of the little bunny running away from home in different and unique ways, is displayed in color as they make the situations stand out much more. My favorite image in the book would be the image of the mother bunny posing as the wind and blowing her child, who is a sailboat at this point, towards the destination she desires.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496449882i/22914327._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="Bunny" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The reason why I took off half a point from the rating was because even though the book is showing that the mother bunny truly does care for her child by following him to the ends of the earth whenever the little bunny runs away, I cannot help but feel like the mother bunny’s behavior comes off as a bit like a stalker as she would chase her child no matter where he goes. Just like Robert Munsch’s children’s book “Love You Forever,” while it is cute that the mother bunny cares enough for her child to chase him down across the earth, the whole “the mother bunny is going to catch her son no matter what” theme might be unsettling for some readers to handle.<br><br>Overall, “The Runaway Bunny” is a cute story about the power of love shared between a parent and their child that many children will enjoy for many years! I would recommend this book to children ages four and up, even though the stalker implications of the mother bunny might unsettle some readers.<br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2017/06/the-runaway-bunny-by-margaret-wise-brown.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406978887i/10622960._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="Banner" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15439802398341904996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer337764620164318338"><br/>My darling Jess decided to run away as a tot. Always the independent sort, the rules of the house were getting to her. Don't clunk your brother on the head, don't steal cookies, don't glue the cat to the floor, the usual. She packed a backpack, put on all her accessories (she was quite into a tiara and lots of beads back then) and set off. I was being the free to be you and me mom I tried to be when not hollering at my children - so I kept my distance and let her leave. With me shadowing her. It</span>
  <span id="freeText337764620164318338" style="display:none"><br />My darling Jess decided to run away as a tot. Always the independent sort, the rules of the house were getting to her. Don't clunk your brother on the head, don't steal cookies, don't glue the cat to the floor, the usual. She packed a backpack, put on all her accessories (she was quite into a tiara and lots of beads back then) and set off. I was being the free to be you and me mom I tried to be when not hollering at my children - so I kept my distance and let her leave. With me shadowing her. It was cute until we came to the block and she was planning on crossing the street alone. I asked her where she was planning on going and she waved towards the distance(surprisingly towards the right direction) and announced she was going to I-95 and walk to her grandma's. <br /><br />Yeah.<br /><br />We read a lot of this book in our house. Children seem to get this book more often than adults on first read. It is a book of great comfort to those who have a restless heart. </span>

<div id="review_420439440" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420439440" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/207973-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302175671p2/207973.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420439440?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/207973-emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420439440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8010897974773608606">This isn't one I'll be reading to my kids. Wherever you go, your mother will find you, so just stay home and eat a carrot? No thanks. Also, the things the mother changes into to find her bunny are often controlling: a fisherman to his fish; a wind to his sailboat; a gardener to his crocus. If it's about unconditional love, which I think it is, the things they change into could have better supported this message. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3877987997687295166">This book is forever close to my heart.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/58922.The_Runaway_Bunny' title='The Runaway Bunny by Margaret Wise Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Runaway Bunny</a> is still a book that I think about often. Given my love of rabbits growing up, an now, it's a book that my mom bought for me and read to me early on. I was her little bunny, and no matter what she would always be there for me. The book is about the safety of home and the love of a mother. It's about knowing that your family will be there for you no matter what, supporting you, loving you, thinking of you. It's a beautiful story, and a bea</span>
  <span id="freeText3877987997687295166" style="display:none">This book is forever close to my heart.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/58922.The_Runaway_Bunny" title="The Runaway Bunny by Margaret Wise Brown" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Runaway Bunny</a> is still a book that I think about often. Given my love of rabbits growing up, an now, it's a book that my mom bought for me and read to me early on. I was her little bunny, and no matter what she would always be there for me. The book is about the safety of home and the love of a mother. It's about knowing that your family will be there for you no matter what, supporting you, loving you, thinking of you. It's a beautiful story, and a beautiful piece of art.<br /><br />As other's asked, why did the bunny want to run away?<br /><br />Kids can be heartless, and we all get like that or at least used to. Essentially, it doesn't matter. In the end he gets his carrot, and knows he's loved. I can't even imagine how many times I traced over the images in this book, and even today I still think about it a lot.<br /><br />My favorite image was the little bunny being a sailboat, and his mother the wind and the clouds.<br /><br />My mom's favorite was the little crocus bunny.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12313557108816116640">Um. Here's another one where I'm reading a different book than everyone else.<br/><br/>You know how people think the song "I'll be watching you" by the Police is romantic? Even though it's about a stalker? This is the picture book equivilent. <br/><br/>A little boy bunny threatens to run away from home and his mother says she will follow him. He suggests magical ways to escape or hide, and she responds. "I will become a flower." "I will become a gardner and find you." I think the little boy is trying to run away be</span>
  <span id="freeText12313557108816116640" style="display:none">Um. Here's another one where I'm reading a different book than everyone else.<br /><br />You know how people think the song "I'll be watching you" by the Police is romantic? Even though it's about a stalker? This is the picture book equivilent. <br /><br />A little boy bunny threatens to run away from home and his mother says she will follow him. He suggests magical ways to escape or hide, and she responds. "I will become a flower." "I will become a gardner and find you." I think the little boy is trying to run away because he feels smothered.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12313557108816116640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Mom bunny says, "No can do, I love you so much that I'll always find you." <br/><br/>Many of her responses are cute, like, "If you become a bird and fly away, I'll be a tree that you can come home to." <br/><br/>Some are weird like, "If you become a flower in a garden, I will become a gardener and I WILL FIND YOU."   <span id="freeText10611821649239913200" style="display:none">A little bunny describes the ways in which he will try to run and hide from his mother. Mom bunny says, "No can do, I love you so much that I'll always find you." <br /><br />Many of her responses are cute, like, "If you become a bird and fly away, I'll be a tree that you can come home to." <br /><br />Some are weird like, "If you become a flower in a garden, I will become a gardener and I WILL FIND YOU." (Caps my own). <br /><br />And some are off-putting like, "If you become a little boat and sail away from me, I'll become the wind and blow you where I want you to go." Why can't the mom be an anchor in a storm, or a safe harbor... or something like that?<br /><br />If you read this with a cute, fun-loving spirit, then probably none of these are weird. But if you are anal and over-analyze like me, then probably some of these will be weird to you.</span>

  <span id="freeText5889322244162829124" style="display:none">I enjoyed this one more, probably because it has a story. <div id="review_960505313" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/960505313" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/303327-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410115829p2/303327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/960505313?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/303327-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/303327-michael?shelf=age-0-5">age-0-5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/303327-michael?shelf=_j-favorites">_j-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/303327-michael?shelf=read-for-children">read-for-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/303327-michael?shelf=_s-favorites_">_s-favorites_</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer960505313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14968420989328563441">Another classic by the author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32929.Goodnight_Moon' title='Goodnight Moon by Margaret Wise Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goodnight Moon</a>. It alternates black and white pages containing conversation between the mother bunny and son bunny, with colorful pages containing no text to emphasize each reunion scene. Reading it recently, I was reminded of another classic, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/370493.The_Giving_Tree' title='The Giving Tree by Shel Silverstein' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Giving Tree</a>, which I really dislike. Whereas they are both about the steadfastness of love, I disliked the "sacrifice everything" message of the Giving Tree. Here, the mother is persistent and steadfast, and tries to me</span>
  <span id="freeText14968420989328563441" style="display:none">Another classic by the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32929.Goodnight_Moon" title="Goodnight Moon by Margaret Wise Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodnight Moon</a>. It alternates black and white pages containing conversation between the mother bunny and son bunny, with colorful pages containing no text to emphasize each reunion scene. Reading it recently, I was reminded of another classic, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/370493.The_Giving_Tree" title="The Giving Tree by Shel Silverstein" rel="nofollow noopener">The Giving Tree</a>, which I really dislike. Whereas they are both about the steadfastness of love, I disliked the "sacrifice everything" message of the Giving Tree. Here, the mother is persistent and steadfast, and tries to meet her baby bunny halfway, with the ultimate goal of doing what she knows is best, not what the bunny wants on a whim.<br /><br />My only complaint is that this book, like hmm, 99%? of children's books, features a mother and son. I know fathers love their children, too, and daughters like to see themselves in the story. Come on publishers! In any case, they are bunnies, so I just change the words to father/son, father/daughter for my non-reading children, and convince them that it could be a father or a mother wearing a dress in the penultimate scene. (It will be a sad day when they learn to read and find how biased the literary world truly is.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14968420989328563441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43845643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6397789602382587604">One of my youngest daughter's favorite bunny stories. She had her own bunny that she took to bed with her every night, originally a lilac colored rabbit which quickly turned grey and shabby. So just as teddy bear stories were her sister's special stories, all the bunny books were usually hers. This one is a delightful, sweet tale about an impish bunny who keeps trying to escape mama bunny, but really only wants to be constantly reassured (as we ALL do!) that he will always be loved and mama will</span>
  <span id="freeText6397789602382587604" style="display:none">One of my youngest daughter's favorite bunny stories. She had her own bunny that she took to bed with her every night, originally a lilac colored rabbit which quickly turned grey and shabby. So just as teddy bear stories were her sister's special stories, all the bunny books were usually hers. This one is a delightful, sweet tale about an impish bunny who keeps trying to escape mama bunny, but really only wants to be constantly reassured (as we ALL do!) that he will always be loved and mama will always come find him. I saw many similiarities between the runaway bunny and my Shell--apparently so did she! Many fond memories... <br />As an extra bonus, I later used this book to teach my Sunday School students about God's unfailing love and His constant search for us. It might as well be a children's version of the well-known poem, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448899.Hound_of_Heaven" title="Hound of Heaven by Francis Thompson" rel="nofollow noopener">Hound of Heaven</a> by Francis Thomas, in that the mama bunny will never let the baby bunny wander so far away that her love cannot find him and bring him back.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6397789602382587604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43574629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11140599084977669871"><br/>I was just rereading this prior to giving it to my sister for her soon-to-be-born baby, and remembered that I was troubled as a child by the bunny son's determination to run away. Didn't it hurt his mother's feelings that he kept wanting to get away from her? <br/><br/>Kids are self-centered little jerks, I guess. <br/><br/>My favorite illustration was the one where the baby bunny is a bird flying and his mother is a tree, like a dryad.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mVvJSu1e+g0jCCTJ2pv30zkXKmlVaAcdf5xeaBT07TXloDph+bKOqDa+qqpHFwcRGhd8jedcsId7RQrvH+W+sw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

The whole Christmas season!\nNow, please don\'t ask why. No one quite knows the reason.&quot;\n\nDr. Seuss\'s small-hearted Grinch ranks right up there with Scrooge when it comes to the crankiest, scowling holiday grumps of all time. For 53 years, the Grinch has lived in a cave on the side of a mountain, looming above the Whos in Whoville. The noisy holiday preparations and infernal singing of the happy little citizens below annoy him to no end. The Grinch decides this frivolous merriment must stop. His &quot;wonderful, awful&quot; idea is to don a Santa outfit, strap heavy antlers on his poor, quivering dog Max, construct a makeshift sleigh, head down to Whoville, and strip the chafingly cheerful Whos of their Yuletide glee once and for all.\n\nLooking quite out of place and very disturbing in his makeshift Santa get-up, the Grinch slithers down chimneys with empty bags and stealing the Whos\' presents, their food, even the logs from their humble Who-fires. He takes the ramshackle sleigh to Mt. Crumpit to dump it and waits to hear the sobs of the Whos when they wake up and discover the trappings of Christmas have disappeared. Imagine the Whos\' dismay when they discover the evil-doings of Grinch in his anti-Santa guise. But what is that sound? It\'s not sobbing, but singing! Children simultaneously adore and fear this triumphant, twisted Seussian testimonial to the undaunted cheerfulness of the Whos, the transcendent nature of joy, and of course, the growth potential of a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14160738848183045433">Margaret Wise Brown wrote hundreds of books and stories during her life, but she is best known for Goodnight Moon and The Runaway Bunny. Even though she died nearly 60 years ago, her books still sell very well.<br/><br/>Margaret loved animals. Most of her books have animals as characters in the story. She liked to write books that had a rhythm to them. Sometimes she would put a hard word into the story or p</span>
  <span id="freeText14160738848183045433" style="display:none">Margaret Wise Brown wrote hundreds of books and stories during her life, but she is best known for Goodnight Moon and The Runaway Bunny. Even though she died nearly 60 years ago, her books still sell very well.<br /><br />Margaret loved animals. Most of her books have animals as characters in the story. She liked to write books that had a rhythm to them. Sometimes she would put a hard word into the story or poem. She thought this made children think harder when they are reading.<br /><br />She wrote all the time. There are many scraps of paper where she quickly wrote down a story idea or a poem. She said she dreamed stories and then had to write them down in the morning before she forgot them.<br /><br />She tried to write the way children wanted to hear a story, which often isn't the same way an adult would tell a story. She also taught illustrators to draw the way a child saw things. One time she gave two puppies to someone who was going to draw a book with that kind of dog. The illustrator painted many pictures one day and then fell asleep. When he woke up, the papers he painted on were bare. The puppies had licked all the paint off the paper.<br /><br />Margaret died after surgery for a bursting appendix while in France. She had many friends who still miss her. They say she was a creative genius who made a room come to life with her excitement. Margaret saw herself as something else - a writer of songs and nonsense.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14160738848183045433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
